root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

Reasons Why You Should Have More Sex\" width=\"540\" height=\"270\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EIt&#x2019;s a well-known fact that most men don&#x2019;t need more reasons to have sex, but how many guys actually stop to think about the fact that sex could play a key role in their overall health and well-being?\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERegular sexual activity is more than recreational; good sexual health is vital to a man&#x2019;s overall physical, psychological and emotional health. Sex can potentially benefit everything from a man&#x2019;s short-term mood, to longer-term issues like cardiovascular health and the reduced risk of prostate cancer.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn addition, sex is a cost-effective and enjoyable way to ensure your long-term health. It&#x2019;s cheaper than a gym membership and a lot better for your waistline than a nightly six pack. With the average man being more mindful than ever about both his budget and his health, sex might be just what the doctor ordered.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EHere are 5 reasons sex makes men healthier &#x2013; so get busy tonight.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Ch2\u003E1. Calorie Burn\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E While sex alone may not be enough to create bulging&#xA0;biceps and washboard abs, intercourse definitely gets the blood pumping by raising the heart rate and burning calories. Estimates show that an average session between the sheets can burn 85 to upwards of 200 calories in 30 minutes. If you spent half an hour having sex daily, that could lead to a weight loss of 10 pounds or more over the course of a year. And it&#x2019;s hopefully more fun than a run on the treadmill. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated\u003Ci\u003E:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.askmen.com\u002Ftop_10\u002Fdating\u002Fbest-sex-positions.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003ETop 10 Best Sex Positions\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E2. Strength Training\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E In addition to burning calories, sex aids in testosterone production, which can strengthen bones and muscles. Testosterone is also responsible for maintaining healthy energy levels, mood, fertility, and sexual desire. So having sex today could help keep your sex drive up down the road. Decreasing testosterone levels, known as andropause or male menopause, can result in a number of side effects including decreased libido, fatigue and depression, among others.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ci\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.askmen.com\u002Fdating\u002Flove_tip\u002F59_love_tip.html\"\u003E7 Sexual Positions Women Enjoy \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E3. Cancer Prevention\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E A number of studies show that men who ejaculate on a regular basis are more than 30% less likely to develop&#xA0;prostate cancer. &#xA0;Regular ejaculation, whether from intercourse or masturbation, help flush out the prostate, which may help curb the development of prostate cancer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E4. Improved Cardiovascular Health\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E Because sex is a good form of exercise, it makes sense that it would positively impact the health of your heart. A study from Queens University shows that men who have sex more than three times a week cut their risk of heart attack and stroke in half. Sex has also been shown to lower blood pressure, which further accounts for the overall positive impact on cardiovascular health. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.askmen.com\u002Ftop_10\u002Fdating\u002Fsex-basics.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Sex Basics To Up Your Bedroom Game\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E5. Stress Relief\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E The decreased blood pressure that can result from sex could help lower your stress level. Various study participants have been shown to have a smaller rise in blood pressure during stressful situations after sex, as compared to other test subjects. Moreover, sex releases feel-good endorphins that can help lower anxiety. Bans in Soccer May Not be Enough to Stop Concussions","summary":"Outlawing heading the ball during soccer games may reduce the rate of concussions, but eliminating player-on-player contact would help more, suggests a new study.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fc7c7cfb8d4f97e864299648b66f12a9bc43b7b13.jpg\" alt=\"&#x2018;Heading&#x2019; Bans in Soccer May Not be Enough to Stop Concussions\" width=\"540\" height=\"810\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELi Dongna of China and Alex Morgan of the United States go up for a header in the second half in the FIFA Women&#x2019;s World Cup 2015 Quarter Final match at Lansdowne Stadium on June 26, 2015 in Ottawa, Canada.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo by Jana Chytilova\u002FFreestyle Photo\u002FGetty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOutlawing &#x201C;heading the ball&#x201D; during \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E games may reduce the rate of concussions, but eliminating player-on-player contact would help more, suggests a new study.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe findings challenge recent calls to ban &#x201C;heading,&#x201D; which is when players hit \u003Ca\u003Esoccer&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eballs with their heads, the study&#x2019;s lead author told Reuters Health.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F07\u002F02\u002Fsports\u002Fsoccer\u002Fwomens-world-cup-semifinal-injuries-morgan-brian-alexandra-popp.html\"\u003Eheading debate\u003C\u002Fa\u003E sprang back into action after Morgan Brian of the U.S. and Alexandra Popp of Germany cracked heads while both attempting to head the ball in a Woman&#x2019;s World Cup semifinal game. Both were visibly injured, but deemed well enough to quickly return to playing in the game by their team doctors &#x2014; and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F07\u002F02\u002Fsports\u002Fsoccer\u002Fwomens-world-cup-semifinal-injuries-morgan-brian-alexandra-popp.html\"\u003Ereignited conversation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that the&#xA0;F&#xE9;d&#xE9;ration Internationale de Football Association (FIFA) is not doing enough to protect its players.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Intuitively it sounds great,&#x201D; said \u003Ca\u003EDawn Comstock\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of \u003Ca\u003EColorado School of Public Health\u003C\u002Fa\u003E at the \u003Ca\u003EUniversity of Colorado\u003C\u002Fa\u003E Anschutz Medical Campus in Aurora. &#x201C;It even has the word &#x2018;head&#x2019; in it.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EComstock and her colleagues report in JAMA Pediatrics that players are more likely to get concussions during heading than other \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E plays, but it&#x2019;s not the cause of the\u003Ca\u003Einjuries\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;When you look more deeply in the data, it&#x2019;s not the act of athletes hitting the balls with their heads at all,&#x201D; Comstock said. &#x201C;Rather, it&#x2019;s athlete-to-athlete contact that occurs during heading.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Safer \u003Ca\u003ESoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E campaign, promoted by the nonprofit \u003Ca\u003EBoston\u003C\u002Fa\u003E-based \u003Ca\u003ESports Legacy Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, urges that heading be delayed until high school or age 14. The campaign is backed by professional \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E players.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo see if the data support a ban on heading, the researchers studied a representative sample of U.S. high school \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E players. Overall, between 2005 and 2014, 627 concussions occurred during 1,393,753 \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E practices or competitions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPlayer-on-player contact was the most common cause of concussions overall, they found.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHeading was the most common \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E-related play associated with concussions, compared to other plays like passing or defending the ball. Heading accounted for about 31 percent of concussions among boys and about a quarter of concussions among girls.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut about 78 percent and about 62 percent of heading-relate concussions among boys and girls, respectively, were due to contact with another player.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile some young players do get concussions when they head the ball, that number is very small compared to those who are injured by another player while heading the ball, Comstock said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe current rules of \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in many leagues reduce player-to-player contact, she said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;If we just enforce those kind of rules to eliminate or at least reduce athlete-to-athlete impacts, that would do more to reduce concussions than just banning heading alone,&#x201D; Comstock said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDr. \u003Ca\u003ERobert Cantu\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, co-founder and medical director of the \u003Ca\u003ESports Legacy Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, told Reuters Health that the new study confirms previous research on the rate of concussion during heading.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;What (Comstock) does point out - and she&#x2019;s looking at the high school level not the youth level - is that rough play also needs to be addressed,&#x201D; said Cantu, who was not involved with the new study. His organization supports that, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fhow-to-overcome-depression-after-a-sports-injury-92559471297.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EHow to Overcome Depression After a Sports Injury\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHeading is still the activity with the highest incidence, he pointed out. Also, under age 14 is when the maximum development of the brain occurs.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;By banning headers before (age) 14 we can take 30 percent of concussions down to zero overnight,&#x201D; said Christopher Nowinski, the \u003Ca\u003ESports Legacy Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2019;s co-founder and executive director.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDr. \u003Ca\u003EJeffrey Bazarian\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of the \u003Ca\u003EUniversity of Rochester\u003C\u002Fa\u003E Medical Center in New York also cautioned that it would be difficult to know how many concussions could be prevented by enforcing current rules.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;When two players go up for a head ball, they&#x2019;re both following the rules,&#x201D; said Bazarian, who wasn&#x2019;t involved with the new research.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHe stressed that concussions are treatable, and the real question is how repeated hits to players&#x2019; heads impact them later on.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe authors also note out that most \u003Ca\u003Einjuries\u003C\u002Fa\u003E reported in \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E are to lower parts of the body, not the head.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next:&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca Shockingly Harrowing Details of Bunion Surgery","summary":"It began with a bunion on my left foot. Its my mothers fault, I muttered to myself. If she hadnt insisted on my taking those black, slingback shoes that looked like Jimmy Choo knock offs, my foot would not look the way it did.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F4244687a62676e00514fb51fcaf634c93b4a54ed.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"720\" alt=\"The Shockingly Harrowing Details of Bunion Surgery\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThree weeks on crutches, 8 weeks in special shoes, and only washing your feet once weekly during that time? Who knew? One woman shares her story of bunion surgery.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt began with a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fhealth-wellness\u002Farticles\u002F2015\u002F06\u002F01\u002F5-embarrassing-foot-conditions-and-what-you-can-do-about-them\" title=\"Link: null\"\u003Ebunion on my left foot\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s my mother&#x2019;s fault,&#x201D; I muttered to myself. If she hadn&#x2019;t insisted on my taking those black, slingback shoes that looked like Jimmy Choo knock offs, my foot would not look the way it did.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI conveniently forgot I had a choice and didn&#x2019;t have to accept, much less wear the shoes in the first place, regardless of how they accentuated my already shapely calves.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESlowly, I watched my large left toe migrate toward the second toe, and in the process, the joint in the big toe kept moving outward. When the orb became red and caused pain while walking, I knew it was time to see an orthopedic foot surgeon. Two weeks and two X-rays later, the surgeon explained the procedure, including the recuperation period, which would be three weeks on crutches, keeping the foot dry and a total of eight weeks in a special &#x201C;bunion&#x201D; shoe. I hoped they at least came in multiple color choices.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThere would be six weekly visits after the stitches were removed for routine dressing changes. I had to resist the urge to wrinkle my nose at the thought of not bathing my foot for eight weeks, and the pungent odor that would permeate the air around my healing apendage. The surgeon assured me foot cleansing would be performed by his assistant when the bandages were changed. I felt better knowing proper foot hygiene would occur at least once a week during that time period.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F0ef7c2f70f6e7ad238a22c588980789b9d5f1243.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAn x-ray of feet with bunions.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMy first \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Farticles\u002F2015\u002F03\u002F13\u002Frecovery-from-bunion-surgery-faster-than-in-past\"\u003Ebunionectomy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E was performed six weeks later. I woke up in pain, vaguely conscious my left foot felt unnaturally bulky. Miraculously, modern medicine intervened in the form of a narcotic injection, and I fell into a drug-induced sleep. What seemed like only moments later, I was told it was time to dress and go home; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Farticles\u002F2014\u002F08\u002F29\u002Ftake-steps-to-control-bunions\"\u003Ebunion correction\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is a same-day procedure. I barely remember being escorted to my friend&#x2019;s car or the ride home.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELinda fed me soup and crackers, put me to bed and stayed with me in case I needed assistance getting up during the night. I was grateful she was such a good friend. Burning, throbbing pain woke me the next morning. Medication intended to ease the pain, upset my empty stomach and promptly came back up. Linda blanched visibly, handed me a wastebasket, promptly told me I was on my own and was out the door. Appreciative thoughts exited with her departure. The rest of the day was spent alone, in a pain-induced fog. Fear of another nausea attack stopped me from taking the medication. Who would empty the wastebasket? Phone calls between doctors followed, as I pleaded to go to the hospital for observation. No one seemed to know who had the authority to admit me &#x2013; the surgeon or my primary care physician. Late at night the impasse broke, and permission was granted for admission.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFrustration with the after hours, snail-like pace of admission procedures provided the perfect opportunity to hone my skill of yelling at the top of my lungs. Linda tried to distract me by doing her imitation of an elk in rutting season, which always induced fits of laughter. It did. Briefly. I promptly resumed voicing my displeasure several octaves higher than before, hoping this behavior would get someone to at least acknowledge my existence and alleviate my pain. I was hoarse from yelling by the time that finally happened.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI spent two days in the hospital receiving narcotic medication and sleeping \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fpatient-advice\u002Fslideshows\u002F12-questions-to-ask-before-discharge\"\u003Ebefore being discharged\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Once again, Linda drove me home.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor the following two weeks, I reclined on the couch, my foot encased in the boring, black bunion shoe, elevated higher than my heart, watching E-Hollywood, Lifetime and A&amp;E on television. The following week I was back at my desk, and six weeks later, wearing regular shoes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA year and a half later, I had a d&#xE9;j&#xE0; vu experience as I looked at my right foot. It was beginning to resemble the left foot prior to surgery. I knew the same fate had befallen my right foot, and another bunionectomy was just a footprint away. &#x201C;I&#x2019;ll bounce back faster if I have surgery now instead of waiting until I&#x2019;m older,&#x201D; I reasoned. Being slightly vain and wanting to have a matched set, I again saw the surgeon for a consultation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFour weeks later, a bunionectomy was performed on my right foot. Before the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fpatient-advice\u002Farticles\u002F2014\u002F07\u002F28\u002Fare-you-getting-the-right-anesthetic\"\u003Eanesthetic\u003C\u002Fa\u003E took effect, I commented on the music in the operating room and requested acoustic guitar be played during surgery. Please, no country\u002Fwestern. I woke up in the recovery room and then again in Pod C, where I spent the next couple hours until the effects of the spinal wore off. A few hours later, I was home, resting on the couch. My recuperation was the same, and the routine didn&#x2019;t bother me the first several days.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps because it was spring and the sun beckoned, I was restless. Sitting on the couch gave me ample time to notice the lint on the rugs, dust in the corners and dirt on the linoleum kitchen floor. I had cleaned before the surgery, but dirt and dust have lives of their own and seem to take the commandment\u003Ci\u003Ebe fruitful and multiply\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ci\u003E \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eseriously.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBeing mobility challenged was no excuse to compromise my cleaning standards. I figured out a way to vacuum on crutches. Using the vacuum cleaner as one crutch, and the other crutch under my right arm, I slowly maneuvered the vacuum on the carpet, cleaning small sections at a time, trying hard to avoid bumping into the furniture. I had to stop every few feet to move the crutch that wasn&#x2019;t being used, and position it along the wall. The muscles in my upper torso were getting toned from this workout, as were the muscles in my upper arms from using crutches. &#x201C;I&#x2019;ll be buff in no time,&#x201D; I thought.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENext came &#x201C;combing&#x201D; the fringe on the area rugs. This required balancing and bending my good leg, holding both crutches on the hand rest with my right arm and leaning forward with the vacuum attachment. When one area of the fringe was &#x201C;coiffed,&#x201D; I hopped to the next section until the fringe was perfectly straight. After my workout, I collapsed on the couch, feeling as if I&#x2019;d just scaled one of the seven peaks, too exhausted to appreciate my accomplishment. When Linda came to visit I admonished her to step over the fringe so as not to disturb its symmetry. She threw me a pathetic look.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENow, 20-plus years later, and foot surgery trials a dim memory. I love \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Farticles\u002F2012\u002F06\u002F14\u002Fpedicure-or-pedicurse-proceed-with-caution\"\u003Eshowing off my feet\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in a pair of slinky, snappy sandals with \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fhealth-wellness\u002Farticles\u002F2013\u002F10\u002F07\u002Ffoot-health-101-learn-how-to-treat-your-feet\" title=\"Link: http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fhealth-wellness\u002Farticles\u002F2013\u002F10\u002F07\u002Ffoot-health-101-learn-how-to-treat-your-feet\"\u003Eno unsightly bunions\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to mar their beauty. I&#x2019;ll never again have \u003Ci\u003Ebunion blues\u003C\u002Fi\u003E! I only have \u003Ci\u003Etwo\u003C\u002Fi\u003E feet!\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E- By Lois Fink&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELois Fink is an inspirational speaker, patient advocate and published writer. src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Ff442c2a5f1870d2c3b32ba66acac27794aa58986.jpg\" alt=\"Trying to Lose Weight? 8 Things You Should Be Doing at Work (Yes, Right at Your Desk)\" width=\"540\" height=\"720\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYour chair could really be messing up your posture.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo:&#xA0;Bill&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003EDiodato\u003C\u002Fi\u003E)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETreadmill desks have been gaining popularity again among women with offices&#x2014;and deep pockets. And while they definitely can help increase your physical activity at the office, a recent study shows that they have one major drawback: decreased productivity. We found eight less distracting items to add to your office (or cubicle) if you&#x2019;re looking to stay active and lose weight this summer.&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E1. Keep a scale under your desk. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EAnd we highly suggest you make it a smart scale. Step on the Withings smart body analyzer, $149.95, when you walk into work, then peruse its collected data&#x2014;your weight and body fat measurements, Body Mass Index, pulse, air quality, weight history, and more&#x2014;as you go through your work-related emails. The scale will use your office&#x2019;s Wi-Fi to send stats directly to your inbox!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E2. Swap your office chair for a stability ball.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Balancing on a blown-up ball engages your core and back, but more important, it keeps you moving, says Heather Milton, MS, clinical exercise physiologist at the Center for Musculoskeletal Care at NYU Langone Medical Center. &#x201C;You&#x2019;re shifting more than when you&#x2019;re simply sitting in a chair, which keeps you from being completely sedentary,&#x201D; she explains. Consider splurging on Gaiam&#x2019;s custom fit balance ball chair ($79.98), which gives you the option of placing the ball into a stabilized, ergonomic chair when your abs need relief.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002Fblogs\u002Fsmitten\u002F2015\u002F06\u002Fsigns-he-is-in-love-men-boyfriend?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E25 Unmistakable Signs He&#x2019;s in Love With You\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E2. &#x2026;or lose your chair entirely.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E &#x201C;Stand while you&#x2019;re on a phone call, or initiate a standing meeting,&#x201D; suggests Milton. (Note: \u003Ci\u003EGlamour\u003C\u002Fi\u003E staffers have a stand-up meeting every morning.) Not only will these activities kick your metabolism into high gear, they&#x2019;ll &#x201C;actually increase productivity, because you&#x2019;re increasing your blood flow, which increases your cognitive focus,&#x201D; says Milton.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E3. Use a swivel footrest.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E It&#x2019;s a great idea to prop your feet on a footrest for simple ergonomics. But selecting one such as the Webble ($149.99), which tilts, turns, and slides, keeps your lower body busy and your metabolism high&#x2014;like you would on a treadmill&#x2014;without losing your breath or focus.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E4. Stash sneakers under your desk. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EYou won&#x2019;t be able to pop into that last-minute rowing class when you find yourself leaving work early&#x2014;unless you&#x2019;re prepared. So, &#x201C;decrease all the obstacles that prevent you from being active,&#x201D; says Milton. &#x201C;The bottom drawer of my filing cabinet is filled with workout clothes and sneakers.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E5. Set a timer. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#x201C;The longer you sit, the greater your risk of developing a cardiac disease or metabolic disease, or increasing your weight,&#x201D; says Milton. Remind yourself to get moving&#x2014;even if it&#x2019;s just for a walk to the water fountain&#x2014;with a timer from the kitchen aisle at your local grocery store. Or download free app Lark, which tracks your activities and prompts you to move with specific tips such as, &#x201C;Your seat could probably use a rest. You haven&#x2019;t moved in over an hour!&#x201D; If you have an Apple Watch, this feature is built in.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002F2008\u002F09\u002F10-things-hes-thinking-when-youre-naked?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Things He&#x2019;s Thinking When You&#x2019;re Naked\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E6. Get handy. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EOK, this one has nothing to do with weight loss, but it&#x2019;s important for your health. If you type on a keyboard for long stretch of time, give your hands, wrists, and tendons some relief. Even if you&#x2019;re not worried about carpal tunnel syndrome right now, you can still benefit from stretches or some specialized tech. Try: Clinically Fit Inc.&#x2019;s hand exerciser ($30), a glove-like tool that will build strength and flexibility from your fingers to your elbows. Slip it on here and there to help keep your muscles loose.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E7. Tighten down below. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EWhether you&#x2019;re on the phone, in a meeting, or typing up a report, you can do kegels or butt clenches&#x2014;try holding each muscle for 15 seconds before releasing for maximum results&#x2014;with no one the wiser!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E8. Take a (workout) break. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EThe \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002F7-min.com\u002F\"\u003Eseven minute workout\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is a super-easy online program that takes nothing more than a wall, chair and&#x2014;you guessed it!&#x2014;seven minutes of your time, making it the perfect plan to work through on your 15 minute afternoon break. Close your office door for privacy, or encourage your cubicle mates to join in. Or, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fhealth-fitness\u002F2015\u002F06\u002Fthe-ultimate-10-minute-office-workout?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003Etry our super-fun 10-minute office workout\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which we created with the team behind popular boutique fitness chain Physique57.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy Jillian href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fcelebrity.yahoo.com\u002Fnews\u002Fjared-padalecki-reveals-struggle-depression-theres-no-shame-203500062-us-weekly.html\"\u003EJared Padalecki\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, who has openly struggled with depression, was overwhelmed at Comic-Con on Sunday when fans paid tribute to his mental health battle. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMore than 7,000 fans lit candles or raised their phone screens in the audience during the question and answer portion of Padalecki&#x2019;s panel. As they raised their &#x201C;candles&#x201D; they shouted, &#x201C;Always keep fighting!&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe message was a reference to the actor&#x2019;s Always Keep Fighting campaign, which was set up to support people struggling with depression, addiction, or suicidal thoughts. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;This is so touching and humbling and honoring,&#x201D; Padalecki told his fans, per Us Weekly. &#x201C;I don&#x2019;t have the proper words to say thank you or how humbled and honored and excited I am and keep it up, guys. Thank y&apos;all so much.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPadalecki later posted the following on Twitter:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"605\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F01df99be327195b96002bbdd051ac43b2ed2f649.png\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFans of the 32-year-old \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002FJared%20Padalecki%20Is%20Overwhelmed%20at%20Comic-Con%20as%20Fans%20Honor%20His%20Bravery%20for%20Talking%20Out%20About%20Depression\"\u003Ewere concerned\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in early May when he sent out cryptic tweets, canceling scheduled appearances.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"510\" height=\"194\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w510\u002F1b3d73c5f42b0a14dd5a447dd1485145509e4fec.png\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHe followed that up with another message:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"515\" height=\"201\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w515\u002F054127dc0e87e4933314fb82f6c937dd6fd04e90.png\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPadalecki recently told Variety that he struggles with depression, and said he began to feel better after taking a step back from his hectic work schedule. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;There&#x2019;s no shame in having to fight every day, but fighting every day, and presumably, if you&#x2019;re still alive to hear these words or read this interview, then you are winning your war. You&#x2019;re here,&#x201D; he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to the Anxiety and Depression Association of America, 3 to 5 percent of people suffer from depression at any given time, and the lifetime risk is 17 percent. The condition is often treated through cognitive behavioral therapy and medication. But while we don&#x2019;t know what type of treatment Padalecki has undergone, if any, outreach from fans seems to have helped on some level. He later issued the following tweet:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"515\" height=\"219\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w515\u002Ff010a05e16529ac6f6b857a51f8b5d62cef3495e.png\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf Padalecki was impacted by positive affirmations, could they be helpful for other people suffering from depression? \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAbsolutely, says clinical psychologist Ben Michaelis, PhD, author of Your Next Big Thing: 10 Small Steps to Get Moving and Get Happy. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthink-your-friend-is-depressed-heres-what-to-say-113885383892.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThink Your Friend Is Depressed? Here&#x2019;s What To Say (And What Not To)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPositive affirmations can help people who are feeling depressed by getting them to change their focus, he tells Yahoo Health: &#x201C;When someone is depressed, nearly all of their mental energy goes toward negative thoughts and feelings. Changing the focus of one&#x2019;s thoughts can have a chain reaction from thoughts to feelings to actions.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPositive feedback can move people with depression along in this chain and help rework the way they perceive the world and themselves, says licensed clinical psychologist Simon Rego, PsyD, director of psychology training at Montefiore Medical Center\u002FAlbert Einstein College of Medicine. Changing a person&#x2019;s thoughts can impact their feelings, he explains, so by hearing more balanced and self-affirming thoughts as well as thinking them, a person can often feel better as a result.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F15-myths-and-facts-about-suicide-and-depression-94537114763.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E15 Myths and Facts About Suicide and Depression\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHow can you tell if someone is clinically depressed? Rego tells Yahoo Health that someone is typically depressed if he or she has symptoms for at least two weeks (including difficulty sleeping, appetite changes, low energy, and thoughts of life not being worth living) and these symptoms have an impact on the ability to function at home, at work, or socially.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHave a loved one struggling with depression? In addition to encouraging them to seek treatment, Rego says there are several types of affirmations you can provide that can help: \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Col\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EValidating statements: Trying to let the person know how hard it must be for them, and that their problems are real.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EAccepting statements: Letting the person know that you&#x2019;re there for them no matter what.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EEncouraging statements: Gently pushing the person to keep trying, despite how they might feel. \u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EKindness goes a long way, too, Michaelis says: &#x201C;Just letting someone know that you care about them can have a major impact.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fwhat-facebooks-doing-to-help-prevent-suicide-112143733727.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhat Facebook&#x2019;s Doing To Help Prevent Suicide\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! Man Who Lost His Memory at the Dentist","summary":"Root canals are routine, safe procedures right? Wrong.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fc5a10913cc496e41399cd5c92ee412d6a7219102.jpg\" alt=\"The Man Who Lost His Memory at the Dentist\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EEvery dentist patients horror story: leaving with \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eworse \u003Ci\u003Ehealth.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: Andy Sotiriou\u002FGetty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOne morning in March of 2005, William, a British soldier stationed in Germany, woke up and headed to the dentist for a root canal. Ten years have passed, and yet upon waking every morning since that day, William still believes it&#x2019;s March of 2005, that he is a British soldier stationed in Germany, and that he will soon be headed to the dentist for a root canal. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fscienceofus\u002F2015\u002F03\u002Fstrange-case-of-the-woman-haunted-by-dragons.html?mid=yahoohealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Strange Case of the Woman Haunted by Dragons\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESomething, in other words, happened between the time the surgery began and the time it ended &#x2014; something that has prevented him from forming any long-term memories since the day of his dental surgery. When he forms new memories, they now only last about 90 minutes, according to the case report his medical team recently \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov\u002Fpubmed\u002F25978125\"\u003Epublished\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in the journal \u003Ci\u003ENeurocase\u003C\u002Fi\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Patient: \u003C\u002Fb\u003EWilliam was a member of the British Armed Forces, who at 22 married his wife, Samantha, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bbc.com\u002Ffuture\u002Fstory\u002F20150630-my-dentist-saved-my-tooth-but-stole-my-memory\"\u003Eaccording\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to the BBC, though writer David Robson notes that he changed both names to protect the couple&#x2019;s privacy. They have two children, who are now 21 and 18. On a Monday morning in March of 2005, he woke up, went to the gym, stopped in at his office to take care of some emails, and went to the dentist. &#x201C;I remember getting into the chair and the dentist inserting the local anaesthetic,&#x201D; William told Robson. It&#x2019;s the last thing he remembers. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Problem\u003C\u002Fb\u003E: After the surgery, William was pale, and his eyes were &#x201C;vacant&#x201D; and unfocused, his physicians write in the case report. When he hadn&#x2019;t improved by 5 p.m., he was taken to the hospital, where he stayed for three days. There, it became clear that he&#x2019;d somehow lost his ability to form long-term memories; it was like his brain rebooted every ten minutes. While in the hospital, his memory improved a bit, so that he had a &#x201C;90-minute span of awareness,&#x201D; but it has not improved in the ten years that have passed since then. &#x201C;He wakes up believing that he should still be in the military, stationed abroad,&#x201D; the case report authors write. &#x201C;Every day he thinks it is the day of the dental appointment. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fscienceofus\u002F2015\u002F05\u002Fman-who-thought-his-family-was-evil-clones.html?mid=yahoohealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThis Man Thought His Family Was Replaced by Evil Clones\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELike something out of \u003Ci\u003EMemento\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, his wife has entered a guide to his present life in the notes section of his smartphone, titled &#x201C;First thing &#x2014; read this.&#x201D; There, he learns every day what happened to him that day at the dentist, and that his children have now grown into young adults. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Diagnosis: \u003C\u002Fb\u003EWilliam&#x2019;s symptoms would suggest that he has anterograde amnesia, an inability to create new long-term memories, while memories formed before a brain injury are accessible as normal. The cause of injury is a mystery. Imaging scans show no damage to the regions of the brain typically associated with this type of memory loss. Another possibility: Sometimes anterograde amnesia happens after psychological trauma. But William&#x2019;s wife and doctors don&#x2019;t think this quite fits his case, either, as he showed no signs of emotional problems before his memory loss.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDr. Gerald H. Burgess, a clinical psychologist at the University of Leicester and one of the co-authors of the case report, does have a theory, outlined in the BBC write-up of the case: \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOnce we have experienced an event, the memories are slowly cemented in the long term by altering these richly woven networks. That process of &#x201C;consolidation&#x201D; involves the production of new proteins to rebuild the synapses in their new shape; without it, the memory remains fragile and is easily eroded with time. Block that protein synthesis in rats, and they soon forget anything they have just learnt. Crucially, 90 minutes would be about the right time for this consolidation to take place &#x2013; just as William starts to forget the details of the event. Rather than losing its printing press, like Molaison, William&#x2019;s brain seems to have simply run out of ink.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fscienceofus\u002F2015\u002F03\u002Fwoman-whose-brain-gave-her-a-fake-accent.html?mid=yahoohealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Woman Whose Brain Gave Her a Fake Accent\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBurgess hopes that after the publication of the case report, he&#x2019;ll hear from other psychiatrists and neurologists who have seen similar cases, which could eventually help William. Unless that happens, William may live the rest of his life with a memory that erases itself every 90 minutes. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy \u003Ca FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F77f901ba8d854313729baa88b072923566fa681f.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":540,"height":304,"size_type":"original","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FxOfk5RJCF2mmnLoU_VazCqar8aY","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002F40.media.tumblr.com\u002Fe85e7108e1ed32b29141870319bd1eae\u002Ftumblr_inline_nr6r0jGsTy1t1pa1k_540.jpg"}],"highlight_color":"#000000","data_version":"1","title":"Why You Cant Do a Pull-Up","summary":"If your SA isnt working correctly, you are setting up the other 17 muscles that attach to your scapula to fail.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F77f901ba8d854313729baa88b072923566fa681f.jpg\" alt=\"Why You Can&#x2019;t Do a Pull-Up\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EDespite being strong, some people can&#x2019;t figure out how to do a pull-up.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Courtesy of Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Problem\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E Pull-ups are one of those ubiquitous tests of strength, but a move&#xA0;that can humble even the toughest of men. Most who&#xA0;are unable to do this particular feat&#xA0;think the answer lies in more weights. And while your lats, biceps, and traps are doing&#xA0;work during this move, the real answer lies in your serratus anterior (SA), the muscle that holds your shoulder blade against your rib cage. If your SA isn&#x2019;t working correctly, you are setting up the other 17 muscles that attach to your scapula to fail. When the scapula is out of position, you are putting yourself at a mechanical disadvantage. In other words, it&#x2019;s not strength, it&#x2019;s positioning.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mensjournal.com\u002Fexpert-advice\u002Fthe-only-8-moves-you-need-to-be-fit-20140306?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=pullup\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Only 8 Moves You Need to Be Fit\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs a physical therapist, I am always amazed to see how much strength is trapped in the body because bones are out of position. When I put the bones back in to the right position, the muscles are at the right length, and all of a sudden, the body moves better. You may be strong, but you are always stronger in balance and in alignment.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis is especially true for the strength and balance required to do a pull-up. Put the scapula in the right position, and your lower trap, biceps, and lats will work much better. With the scapula out of position, you are asking your teres major and minor (which are tiny muscles) and only a portion of your lat to lift your entire body. No wonder you can&#x2019;t get your chin up to the bar.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mensjournal.com\u002Fhealth-fitness\u002Fexercise\u002Fthe-perfect-pull-up-20140131?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=pullup\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EHow to Do a Perfect Pull-Up\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Solution\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E You need to start releasing muscles that attach to your shoulder. Modern life is about texting, working on the computer, and stuffing yourself into airplane seats built for 12 year old kids. The result is a forward head and rounded shoulders and ultimately, a shoulder blade that is constantly drifting forward and up. Gravity exacerbates the situation, pulling you down and further out of position.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mensjournal.com\u002Fhealth-fitness\u002Fexercise\u002Fhow-to-fix-the-shoulder-slump-20150703?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=pullup\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EHow to Fix the Shoulder Slump\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHere&#x2019;s what you need to do. Get a lacrosse ball and then get to work. First release your pec muscles, then the teres (those little guys on the outside of your scapula that are working so hard to get you over that bar), and finally the upper trap. For the pec and teres, place the lacrosse ball on a tender spot and lean up against a wall. Lean a tolerable amount of weight onto the ball, then move your arm back and forth. For the trap, you want to find a bar bell, get underneath it so your upper trap is, well, trapped underneath it, shrug up and depress your shoulder. For each release, you will know it is working when your body starts to melt into the lacrosse ball or barbell.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThen I have some strengthening for you to do:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E1.&#xA0;\u003Cb\u003ELower Trap RDLs:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;Holding two dumbbells (or a barbell), stand with your weight on your heels and knees slightly bent and forced out. Your feet should be turned out at a 10&#x2013;15 degree angle. Keep your palms forward, pinch your shoulder blades down and back, and squeeze your glutes. Slowly hinge at the hips, keeping your back flat and shoulder blades down and back.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESlide the weights down, keeping them just in front of your shins, but not touching. Go down as far as you can without starting to slouch (ideally a 90-degree angle) then slowly hinge back up to the start position. The weights you use should be light enough that you can maintain good form but heavy enough to challenge you during the exercise.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mensjournal.com\u002Fexpert-advice\u002F5-moves-to-beat-back-pain-20141216?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=pullup\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Only 5 Moves You Need for a Healthy Back\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E 2.&#xA0;\u003Cb\u003EDownward Dog Push-Up:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;In a push-up position, lift hips toward the ceiling forming an upside down V shape. Be sure the back is straight and both legs are straight with the heels touching the floor. Both hands should be splayed and facing outward. With both arms straight, push into the ground so as to open up the armpits.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E In this position bend at the elbows, lowering your head to the ground, then push back to starting position.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mensjournal.com\u002Fhealth-fitness\u002Fexercise\u002F10-ways-to-do-a-push-up-20140708?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=pullup\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Ways to Do a Push-Up\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E3.&#xA0;\u003Cb\u003EScapular Stabilization Push-ups:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;Place dumbbells on floor, about three inches outside shoulders, turned outward at 45-degree angles. Start in a raised position, abs and glutes engaged, back flat, and head at a neutral position. Punch forward with shoulders to engage serratus anterior.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESlowly lower toward floor, stopping when elbows reach a 90-degree angle. Raise to starting position. Repeat.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mensjournal.com\u002Fexpert-advice\u002Fthe-11-best-shoulder-exercises-20150312?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=pullup\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe 11 Best Shoulder Exercises\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4.&#xA0;\u003Cb\u003ESerratus Anterior&#xA0;Stabilization Push-ups:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;Place dumbbells on floor, about three inches outside shoulders, perpendicular to the body. Start in a raised position, abs and glutes engaged, back flat, and head at a neutral position. Punch forward with shoulders to engage serratus anterior.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESlowly lower toward floor, stopping when elbows reach a 90-degree angle. Raise to starting position. Repeat.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy David Reavy\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca Is It So Hard to Get a Lyme Disease Diagnosis?","summary":"She says that some misdiagnosed her symptomsdebilitating pain and fatigueas chronic fatigue syndrome or depression.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fc074414115edaa784f3d302f80e66fb606d324a5.jpg\" alt=\"Why Is It So Hard to Get a Lyme Disease Diagnosis?\" width=\"540\" height=\"296\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAll patients of Lyme seem to have one thing in common - it was so hard to diagnose. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAvril Lavigne opened up again recently about her struggle with Lyme disease, a tick-borne illness she says left her bedridden for months and desperate for answers. The 30-year-old singer told Good Morning America that she saw many doctors and underwent a battery of tests in the last year, but that it wasn&#x2019;t until she found a Lyme disease specialist that she was given a correct diagnosis.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I was in Los Angeles, literally, like the worst time in my life and I was seeing, like, every specialist and literally, the top doctors. It&#x2019;s so stupid,&#x201D; Lavigne said in an interview televised yesterday. She says that some misdiagnosed her symptoms&#x2014;debilitating pain and fatigue&#x2014;as chronic fatigue syndrome or depression, while others told her she was simply dehydrated or exhausted from touring.\u003Cbr\u003E&#x201C;This is what they do to a lot of people who have Lyme disease,&#x201D; she said. &#x201C;They don&#x2019;t have an answer for them so they tell them, like, &#x2018;You&#x2019;re crazy.&#x2018;&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELavigne began to suspect she had Lyme disease&#x2014;the number-one insect-borne disease in the United States&#x2014;a few months after she began feeling exhausted and lightheaded. Her symptoms eventually got so bad she felt like she couldn&#x2019;t breathe, talk, or move. &#x201C;I thought I was dying,&#x201D; she told People in April.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.health.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fgallery\u002F0,,20834752,00.html?xid=yahoo-lyme-070615\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E15 Diseases Doctors Often Get Wrong&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo why did it take so long for Lavigne to get answers? And could her experience happen to others, as well?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFortunately, most cases of Lyme disease are caught and treated much earlier, says Anne R. Bass, MD, a rheumatologist at the Hospital for Special Surgery in New York City, and this degree of misdiagnosis isn&#x2019;t very common. But pinpointing this type of infection is not an exact science, and symptoms are not always crystal clear.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Many people will develop a bulls-eye rash, which makes it fairly easy to diagnose,&#x201D; she says. But this telltale symptoms is sometimes faint or on hidden parts of the body, and some people don&#x2019;t get one at all.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Other early symptoms, like fever or aches and pains, could be attributed to a virus or flu,&#x201D; says Bass. &#x201C;So if you don&#x2019;t see a rash, you might not even go to the doctor&#x2014;or it&#x2019;s possible your doctor might not recognize it.&#x201D; (Some Lyme disease cases go away on their own, she adds, so it&#x2019;s possible to have had it and never known.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.health.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fgallery\u002F0,,20352008,00.html?xid=yahoo-lyme-070615\"\u003E13 Conditions That Mimic Fibromyalgia\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMost physicians, especially those who practice in tick hot-spots like the northeastern United States, know to look out for Lyme disease symptoms during spring and summer months. But the disease is less prevalent in Southern California, where Lavigne says she was seeking treatment. If a patient hasn&#x2019;t had a rash and doesn&#x2019;t remember being bitten, doctors there may be slower to identify ticks as a potential factor.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBass says that anyone who&#x2019;s experienced fatigue or joint pain for several months should think back to when their symptoms started, and whether they spent time in area of the country known for Lyme disease outbreaks. A blood test cannot confirm whether you are currently infected, but it can tell if you have been exposed to Lyme bacterium in the past. (It actually tests for antibodies, which develop a few weeks after a person has been infected and remain in the blood forever.) Doctors can use these test results, along with a person&#x2019;s current symptoms, to make a diagnosis.\u003Cbr\u003E&#x201C;But even these test results can be complex and confusing, especially for physicians who aren&#x2019;t used to dealing with Lyme,&#x201D; Dr. Bass says. Some doctors also believe that Lyme disease can be diagnosed without a positive blood test, she adds&#x2014;although there&#x2019;s no evidence that these methods are accurate or that antibiotics, in these cases, work any better than placebo.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.health.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fgallery\u002F0,,20621010,00.html?xid=yahoo-lyme-070615\"\u003E27 Mistakes Healthy People Make&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E(Lavigne did not reveal exactly how she was diagnosed or whether she tested positive for Lyme antibodies, although she did say she had blood tests when she first became ill.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOnce Lyme disease is diagnosed, two to three weeks of oral antibiotics usually help patients feel better and eliminate all symptoms. If it goes untreated for several months, however, a longer course of drugs&#x2014;usually four weeks&#x2014;is often needed. In extreme cases, antibiotics may also be given through an IV.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBass says that it&#x2019;s uncommon for patients to be prescribed antibiotics for more than a month, even if they continue to experience fatigue and pain. &#x201C;It does take longer for them to get better when there is a delay in diagnosis, but it doesn&#x2019;t really change our duration or course of treatment,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;They may just need to rest and take it easy a bit longer until they have their energy back.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E &#xA0;\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.health.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fgallery\u002F0,,20898778,00.html?xid=yahoo-lyme-070615\"\u003E13 Ways Inflammation Can Affect Your Health\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELavigne is finally feeling better, and says she expects to make a full recovery. That&#x2019;s a good thing, since 10 to 20 percent of people with Lyme disease continue to experience symptoms for months or even years after treatment. This condition is sometimes called chronic Lyme disease, although it&#x2019;s technically known as post-treatment Lyme disease syndrome.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDoctors aren&#x2019;t sure what causes post-Lyme syndrome (some believe that symptoms are due to other tick-borne illnesses, or to chronic conditions like rheumatoid arthritis), and treatments like long-term antibiotic therapy are controversial. But a recent study from Johns Hopkins University showed that one thing is clear: Prolonged Lyme-related illness is more common than was once believed.\u003Cbr\u003E&#x201C;Our data show that many people who have been diagnosed with Lyme disease are in fact going back to the doctor complaining of persistent symptoms, getting multiple tests, and being retreated,&#x201D; the study authors said in a news release. &#x201C;It is clear that we need effective, cost-effective, and compassionate management of these patients to improve their outcomes, even if we don&#x2019;t know what to call the disease.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy Amanda MacMillan\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from Beginners Guide to Spiralizing Your Veggies","summary":"New to spiralizing? Here's what to do  and the best spiralizers on the market.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F209ee65abbe91048d70329c52a18034c17b02e57.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"810\" alt=\"The Beginner&#x2019;s Guide to Spiralizing Your Veggies\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EIf you were hoping spiralizing would go the way of Snackwells, think again. Writer-editor Marjorie Korn makes the case for why now is the perfect time to give it a whirl.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E First off, let&#x2019;s get one thing straight: People who tell you that &#x201C;zoodles&#x201D; (zucchini noodles) are just like pasta are lying. Because pasta is amazing. If it were not for pasta, Leonardo da Vinci may not have painted the Mona Lisa, Giacomo Puccini mightn&#x2019;t have finished Madama Butterfly, and I wouldn&#x2019;t have run a marathon, since the main selling point was carbo-loading. This is not to say that spiralized vegetables are beneath their wheat-based counterpart&#x2014;some sort of dieting consolation prize, like closing your eyes while eating Yoplait yogurt and telling yourself it&#x2019;s lemon meringue pie&#x2014;or a joke on the gluten intolerant. On the contrary, spiralizing is fantastic unto itself. The key is embracing the Spiralifestyle.&#xA0;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EConsider:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EIt&#x2019;s a new medium for vegetables, which we as a country don&#x2019;t eat enough of (a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ers.usda.gov\u002Famber-waves\u002F2014-may\u002Fhealthy-vegetables-undermined-by-the-company-they-keep.aspx#.VYiMx6Zu_R3\"\u003EUSDA survey\u003C\u002Fa\u003E found that most Americans eat their veggies in the form of potatoes and pizza).\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EIt&#x2019;s fun, like nature&#x2019;s throwing you a ticker-tape parade.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003ENow you have something to do with the zucchini that you bought by accident, thinking it was a cucumber.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.giadaweekly.com\u002Fsubscribe.php?utm_source=Yahoo-Health&amp;utm_medium=website&amp;utm_campaign=Subscribe-Oodles-of-Noodles-Article\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWant more Giada? Subscribe to GiadaWeekly.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs far as gadgets go, this one is low-risk. Even the top-of-the-line models don&#x2019;t break the bank. Plus, there isn&#x2019;t a way to reproduce the results with what you&#x2019;ve already got in your kitchen&#x2014;the spin of the spiralizers gives it an edge on your mandolin&#x2019;s julienne feature for these sorts of dishes. Here&#x2019;s my experience with the two main models:\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"810\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F504b9632d4aac5afec40b3f0823d6fb2d888f472.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EMastrad&#x2019;s Deco Vegi Slicer is easy to store and costs less than $15.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you&#x2019;re new to Spiralizing or have a little kitchen, start with a handheld gadget like this Veggetti ($15; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bedbathandbeyond.com\u002Fstore\u002Fproduct\u002Fveggetti-trade-spiral-vegetable-cutter\u002F1042545910?Keyword=vegetti\"\u003Ebedbathandbeyond.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EPros: It&#x2019;s the size of a soda can and easy to use.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n \u003Cli\u003ECons: While it has two teeth sizes, I only venture to use the larger one, since I can never seem to get the smaller one clean. As it is, I&#x2019;ve devoted a toothbrush to cleaning my Spiralizer. And while it&#x2019;s great for long, skinny produce like zucchini, the design won&#x2019;t work on squatter items like beets.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.giadaweekly.com\u002Fview\u002F84c6c8da0ac4941d3b6ee7234315afd1?utm_source=Yahoo-Health&amp;utm_medium=website&amp;utm_campaign=Vegetable-Noodles-Oodles-of-Noodles-Article\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EHow to Make Vegetable Noodles\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F14d5bf271d26e62c121b8b4a23defb6508b6f6c6.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Vegetti is a great starter spiralizer, especially if you have a tiny kitchen.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you have the space and a few more dollars to drop, spring for the Paderno Spiralizer ($50;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.williams-sonoma.com\u002Fproducts\u002Fpaderno-spiralizer-4-blade\u002F?cm_src=AutoSchNullRel\"\u003EWilliams-Sonoma.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EPros: It has multiple blade options that detach for easy cleaning; you end up throwing away less of the vegetable than when using the handheld type; it works with lots of different produce shapes; you can use it to make curly fries.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003ECons: It&#x2019;s bigger than a loaf of bread; you can use it to make curly fries.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.giadaweekly.com\u002Fview\u002F0b3e64ec058b65700afda9e110db74ec?utm_source=Yahoo-Health&amp;utm_medium=website&amp;utm_campaign=Zucchini-Spaghetti-Oodles-of-Noodles-Article\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERecipe: Zucchini Spaghetti with Sun Gold Tomato Sauce\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"432\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F3be16913158e0cf17ce6e450396c3afae70f0858.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Paderno Spiralizer is more versatile and it still won&#x2019;t break the bank.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhichever you choose, you&#x2019;ll use it. A lot. Here are some of my favorite things to do: \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003ESpiralize green and yellow squash and toss the noodles raw with your favorite pasta topper, such as a kale&#x2013;olive oil&#x2013;walnut&#x2013;Pecorino pesto.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n \u003Cli\u003ECook your zoodles: season spiralized zucchini with kosher salt and cook in a medium nonstick pan over medium-high heat, stirring frequently, until the zoodles are soft, 5 minutes; remove from heat, tip out any excess water, and toss with olive oil, freshly ground black pepper, and grated Parmesan.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n \u003Cli\u003ELightly saut&#xE9; spiralized carrots with bean sprouts in sesame oil and place atop an Asian-style veggie burger.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n \u003Cli\u003EIn a mason jar, pack peeled, blanched, and cooled spiralized beets with sliced red onion, garlic, peppercorns, and apple cider vinegar, and refrigerate overnight for pickled beets.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E \n \u003Cli\u003ECurly potatoes, baked or fried, tossed with Old Bay seasoning or barbecue salt.
